  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_e63ae31a-142b-49c8-9c92-8d37f2de0ac8'
      });

</div>


      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer14441978596128485311"><b>Memory makes reality.</b><br/><br/>That's what NYC cop Barry Sutton is learning, as he investigates the devastating phenomenon the media has dubbed False Memory Syndrome—a mysterious affliction that drives its victims mad with memories of a life they never lived.<br/><br/>That's what neuroscientist Helena Smith believes. It's why she's dedicated her life to creating a technology that will let us </span>
  <span id="freeText14441978596128485311" style="display:none"><b>Memory makes reality.</b><br /><br />That's what NYC cop Barry Sutton is learning, as he investigates the devastating phenomenon the media has dubbed False Memory Syndrome—a mysterious affliction that drives its victims mad with memories of a life they never lived.<br /><br />That's what neuroscientist Helena Smith believes. It's why she's dedicated her life to creating a technology that will let us preserve our most precious memories. If she succeeds, anyone will be able to re-experience a first kiss, the birth of a child, the final moment with a dying parent.<br /><br />As Barry searches for the truth, he comes face to face with an opponent more terrifying than any disease—a force that attacks not just our minds, but the very fabric of the past. And as its effects begin to unmake the world as we know it, only he and Helena, working together, will stand a chance at defeating it.<br /><br />But how can they make a stand when reality itself is shifting and crumbling all around them?<br /><br />At once a relentless pageturner and an intricate science-fiction puzzlebox about time, identity, and memory, Recursion is a thriller as only Blake Crouch could imagine it—and his most ambitious, mind-boggling, irresistible work to date.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14441978596128485311" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>
</div>

            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });
      });

//]]>
</script>    </div>
</div>

<div id="review_2666425164" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2666425164" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2666425164?book_show_action=true">Jun 11, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2019">2019</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2666425164" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4689908097443601945"><blockquote>
  <i>But what do you cling to, moment to moment, if memories can simply change. What, then, is real?</i>
</blockquote><br/>Imagine you woke up one morning and discovered that your entire life - your job, your kids, your friends, all your experiences - wasn't real. It still feels real. You remember it vividly. But you also suddenly remember another life; your <i>real</i> life. And you are told that the life you remember is a result of FMS (False Memory Syndrome)-- an illusion created by your brain.<br/><br/>I don't know about you, but t</span>
  <span id="freeText4689908097443601945" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>But what do you cling to, moment to moment, if memories can simply change. What, then, is real?</i>
</blockquote><br />Imagine you woke up one morning and discovered that your entire life - your job, your kids, your friends, all your experiences - wasn't real. It still feels real. You remember it vividly. But you also suddenly remember another life; your <i>real</i> life. And you are told that the life you remember is a result of FMS (False Memory Syndrome)-- an illusion created by your brain.<br /><br />I don't know about you, but that thought is <b>horrifying.</b><br /><br />In this book, New York City cop Barry Sutton investigates the suicide of a woman with FMS. She killed herself after trying to make contact with the husband from her false memories and finding him married with a child. How strange it is that she remembers an entire life with a man who exists, but he doesn't seem to remember her at all. Barry finds himself needing answers.<br /><br />Eleven years earlier, neuroscientist Helena Smith conceives of a technology that can preserve memories and could eventually be a cure for the Alzheimer's that is stealing away her mother's mind. Funded by a mysterious billionaire, Helena builds something that enables people to relive their precious memories. But she never foresees the darker side of the project-- the side that triggers an unraveling of, not only the past, but reality itself.<br /><br />Needless to say, these two stories collide and it is some <b>mind-bendingly awesome stuff</b>. Crouch has written yet another weird, compelling and oddly romantic book. Like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/27833670.Dark_Matter" title="Dark Matter by Blake Crouch" rel="nofollow noopener">Dark Matter</a>, you can expect this book to get bigger and wilder than you ever imagined before even a hint of a solution rears its head. <br /><br />I do also really enjoy how the author brings a lot of heart to these sci-fi thrillers. Sometimes sci-fi books feel a little cold and emotionally-distant, but <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/42046112.Recursion" title="Recursion by Blake Crouch" rel="nofollow noopener">Recursion</a> is ultimately <b>a very emotional and human story</b>. Stories about memories really get to me, because our memories and experiences make us who we are. I <i>am</i> my memories. And one of the saddest things I can think of is not being remembered by someone you love deeply.<br /><br />A thrilling story with very moving moments.<br /><br /><a href="http://emilymay.me" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thebookgeekreviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thebookgeek01" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://instagram.com/emleemay" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/EmilyMayTheBookGeek" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="4689908097443601945" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer1684351364010567350"><b>UPDATE: IT'S OUT!! Go read it so we can all gush about it!!</b><br/><br/>(4.5) As always, Crouch knows how to keep you on your toes and does a great job at mixing thriller and sci-fi genre.<br/><br/>A mysterious disease starts affecting people’s memory, giving them memories of a life they never lived. NYPD detective Barry Sutton is trying to investigated how the False Memory Syndrome is spreading and ultimately will come to face Helena Smith a neuroscientist who invented a device that’s changing the world.<br/><br/>Recursion wil</span>
  <span id="freeText1684351364010567350" style="display:none"><b>UPDATE: IT'S OUT!! Go read it so we can all gush about it!!</b><br /><br />(4.5) As always, Crouch knows how to keep you on your toes and does a great job at mixing thriller and sci-fi genre.<br /><br />A mysterious disease starts affecting people’s memory, giving them memories of a life they never lived. NYPD detective Barry Sutton is trying to investigated how the False Memory Syndrome is spreading and ultimately will come to face Helena Smith a neuroscientist who invented a device that’s changing the world.<br /><br />Recursion will make you question time, memory and life.<br /><br />While the characters and dialogues didn’t grab me from the start, I grew to care about them and their story more and more. By the end, I couldn’t put the book down. <br /><br />The story also became a lot darker than I expected (which I loved!) and the concepts mentioned were fascinating.<br /><br />If you’ve enjoyed Dark Matter by him, I recommend you pick up this one.<br /><br />Can’t wait to see the Netflix adaptation!<br /><br /><i>I received an ARC from the publisher via NetGalley in exchange for an honest review.</i></span>

<div id="review_2708162698" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2708162698" />
    <a title="Nilufer Ozmekik" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/53701594-nilufer-ozmekik"><img alt="Nilufer Ozmekik" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1559807601p2/53701594.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/53701594-nilufer-ozmekik?shelf=best-ones">best-ones</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/53701594-nilufer-ozmekik?shelf=favorite-wtf-mindfu-k-books">favorite-wtf-mindfu-k-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/53701594-nilufer-ozmekik?shelf=can-t-wait-to-read">can-t-wait-to-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/53701594-nilufer-ozmekik?shelf=best-thriller">best-thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/53701594-nilufer-ozmekik?shelf=wtf-i-just-read">wtf-i-just-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2708162698" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer878917359458019708">Congratulations for winning of best sci-fi category from goodreads choice awards 2020! This is one of my favorite books of the year! <br/><br/>Five OMG I’m suffering from brain cells bleeding and explosion of my last standing grey cells, what the hell I just read and who am I ? stars!<br/><br/>I know the drill but let me rephrase one more time! This is not an easy, soft, sunshine and rainbows reading! <br/><br/>In my opinion people who are brave enough to dive into this journey should put themselves an IQ test and discover t</span>
  <span id="freeText878917359458019708" style="display:none">Congratulations for winning of best sci-fi category from goodreads choice awards 2020! This is one of my favorite books of the year! <br /><br />Five OMG I’m suffering from brain cells bleeding and explosion of my last standing grey cells, what the hell I just read and who am I ? stars!<br /><br />I know the drill but let me rephrase one more time! This is not an easy, soft, sunshine and rainbows reading! <br /><br />In my opinion people who are brave enough to dive into this journey should put themselves an IQ test and discover their cognitive skills. ( luckily I read the quantum physics for dummies before the beginning but I feel like I can be great cast for future dumb and dumber movie if they will ever produce the third installment)<br /><br />So this book is amazing combination of time traveling, alternated lifetimes, Minority Reports meet Groundhog Day versus Black Mirror and Back to the Future kinda fascinating science fiction crashes into thriller and romance starting with an effective and memorable suicide attempt scene. <br />A woman suffers from FMS ( false memory syndrome) who thinks her child was being erased, her husband denied her existence so there was nothing better than jump and end her life. But she had small hope in her heart, her husband could come to rescue her but when he didn’t show up, she didn’t want to fight anymore and.... Yes, this book starts with jaw dropping scene and you’re hooked! <br /><br />It’s addictive, unputdownable, nerve damaging, exhausting ride! You wanna know what’s going to happen and think about yourself if I had a chance to save my loved ones by turning back and making my wrongs turn into rights, what would happen! <br /><br />Saving her daughter from the traffic accident, curing your mother’s Alzheimer disease, prevention of school shooting , saving soldiers from the terrorist attacks are just the samples writer show as in alternative realities that have possible to be changed! <br /><br />The difference of Recursion from Dark Matter might be romance parts because I really enjoyed Barry and Helena’s love story. Not only they fought to bring universe into the right pattern but also they fought to get back together to be each other’s final word, everlasting love, end game! <br /><br />This was thrilling, mind bending, provoking book! <br />Dark Matters is going to be Netflix series and I’m already sure that as a brain numbing project, this book finds its place at big screen on near future!<br /><br />Highly recommended, smart, different, unique and exquisite book but not for everyone!<br /><br /><a href="https://niluferozmekik.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">blog</a><br /><a href="https://www.instagram.com/nilylovestoread/" rel="nofollow noopener">instagram</a><br /><a href="https://www.facebook.com/nilufer.ozmekik" rel="nofollow noopener">facebook</a><br /><a href="https://twitter.com/NiluferOzmekik" rel="nofollow noopener">twitter</a></span>

          </span>

<div id="review_2622897173" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2622897173" />
    <a title="Chelsea Humphrey" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/47207032-chelsea-humphrey"><img alt="Chelsea Humphrey" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1585613513p2/47207032.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2622897173?book_show_action=true">Dec 11, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chelsea Humphrey" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chelsea Humphrey" href="/user/show/47207032-chelsea-humphrey">Chelsea Humphrey</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Chelsea by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/67496521-dennis">Dennis</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47207032-chelsea-humphrey?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47207032-chelsea-humphrey?shelf=scared-suspense-reads">scared-suspense-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47207032-chelsea-humphrey?shelf=from-publisher">from-publisher</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2622897173" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7503404110920613763"><b>CONGRATULATIONS- Goodreads Choice Awards Science Fiction Winner!</b><br/><br/>**********************<br/><br/><i>"Everything will look better in the morning. There will be hope again when the light returns. The despair is only an illusion, a trick the darkness plays."</i><br/><br/>I'm convinced that Blake Crouch is <b>THE</b> science fiction/fantasy author of our time. You know, the one that readers pre-order their books without reading the description, the one that 50 years from now people are still talking about, dissecting his plot points </span>
  <span id="freeText7503404110920613763" style="display:none"><b>CONGRATULATIONS- Goodreads Choice Awards Science Fiction Winner!</b><br /><br />**********************<br /><br /><i>"Everything will look better in the morning. There will be hope again when the light returns. The despair is only an illusion, a trick the darkness plays."</i><br /><br />I'm convinced that Blake Crouch is <b>THE</b> science fiction/fantasy author of our time. You know, the one that readers pre-order their books without reading the description, the one that 50 years from now people are still talking about, dissecting his plot points and their dual meanings? Yeah, that's Crouch. <i>If you don't agree, then that's ok, I'll respect your opinion. But also, FIGHT ME.</i> While I've enjoyed all of the author's novels to date, <i>Dark Matter</i> is the one that sealed the deal in making me a life long fan. (But also <i>Desert Places</i>) <i>Recursion</i> is another worthy entry in Crouch's SFF productions, and one that felt reminiscent of <i>Dark Matter</i>, which made me a very happy Chelsea. Yes, the plot is unique in it's own way, but it still gave off those complex vibes that are a cross between "exciting, high concept thriller" and "deep, emotional family drama".<br /><br /><i>"How would I know if one had changed? What would it feel like?"</i><br /> <br />The premise of this novel is simple: <b>What would happen if the memories contained inside your mind had never occurred?</b> I'm not entirely sure how the author devised the plot for this book, but I imagine it stemmed from a simple question, not altogether different from the one presented above. Once you've read the book, it's easy to see how an entire novel could spring from such an innocent thought. It's clear that Crouch has a way with writing sagas that pull the heartstrings, because all of his ideas that evolve into stories are a delicate balance of intellectually stimulating action and moving, emotional love mingled with loss. The kicker is that the author knows how to write a science fiction that seems so dangerously close to reality, you find yourself turning the last page, shaking your head and chuckling because that could NEVER happen, but secretly wondering if it possibly could. <br /><br />If you enjoyed <i>Dark Matter</i> and its extraordinary premise, you'll likely fall head over heels for <i>Recursion</i> as well. A few of the same concepts are used in both novels, but each of these books are truly a labor of love in their own, unique way. Once again, I have found myself floored at how a person's mind could concoct such a brilliant scheme, and I'm looking forward to finding out where Crouch chooses to take us next. <br /><br /><i>*Many thanks to the publisher for providing my review copy.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="7503404110920613763" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2621966018" />
    <a title="Matthew" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16254355-matthew"><img alt="Matthew" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1464987365p2/16254355.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2621966018?book_show_action=true">Jun 20, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Matthew" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Matthew" href="/user/show/16254355-matthew">Matthew</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">All the people!</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=suspense">suspense</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2621966018" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15694396812688197490"><b>Ticking away the moments that make up a dull day<br/>Fritter and waste the hours in an offhand way.<br/>Kicking around on a piece of ground in your home town<br/>Waiting for someone or something to show you the way.<br/><br/>Tired of lying in the sunshine staying home to watch the rain.<br/>You are young and life is long and there is time to kill today.<br/>And then one day you find ten years have got behind you.<br/>No one told you when to run, you missed the starting gun.<br/><br/>Pink Floyd - Time</b><br/><br/>I am just going to say it – Blake Crouch is t</span>
  <span id="freeText15694396812688197490" style="display:none"><b>Ticking away the moments that make up a dull day<br />Fritter and waste the hours in an offhand way.<br />Kicking around on a piece of ground in your home town<br />Waiting for someone or something to show you the way.<br /><br />Tired of lying in the sunshine staying home to watch the rain.<br />You are young and life is long and there is time to kill today.<br />And then one day you find ten years have got behind you.<br />No one told you when to run, you missed the starting gun.<br /><br />Pink Floyd - Time</b><br /><br />I am just going to say it – Blake Crouch is the King of Modern Speculative Science Fiction!<br /><br />Here is your crown, Your Majesty! We are not worthy!<br /><br />Imagine trying to follow up Dark Matter with something just as unique and mind blowing? I think I probably would have just stopped there if I had written it. The apex would have been reached. There is no way I could have topped it. Even trying would probably have fallen flat . . . feeling like I just could not have done any better.<br /><br />To which Emperor Crouch says, “HOLD MY BEER!”<br /><br />Recursion is just as mind blowingly unique as Dark Matter. And, much like Dark Matter I cannot say too much about why it is awesome and mind blowing without ruining it. So, I will give you an idea of in what way it blew my mind by comparing to a scene from an episode of Black Mirror. This comparison will not spoil Recursion, but it will spoil Black Mirror, so I will put it in a spoiler tag. If you have watched all Black Mirror episodes or don’t care about spoilers, you can click it without concern.<br /><br />So, my mind was blown in the same way as <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ the episode where they are trying to get the guy to give details about a crime by interrogating a duplicate version of his consciousness that thinks it is the real him. At the end of the episode, they turn on a Christmas song and leave him locked in a kitchen listening to the song over and over. In the real world they just decide to leave him locked in as a form of torture over the weekend. But, to the trapped consciousness it will feel like billions of years not being able to eat, sleep, or stop listening to the same Christmas song over and over.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Trying to wrap my brain around that scenario is the exact same type of brain wrapping I had going on with this book!<br /><br />If you loved Dark Matter, you must read this!<br /><br />If you love speculative fiction/sci-fi, you must read this!<br /><br />I have no complaints, to me it is just as perfect as I thought Dark Matter was. The only downside is now I will have to wait a long time to see what King Crouch will do next!</span>

<div id="review_2622956296" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2622956296" />
    <a title="Melissa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9684061-melissa"><img alt="Melissa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528750408p2/9684061.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2622956296?book_show_action=true">Jun 17, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melissa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melissa" href="/user/show/9684061-melissa">Melissa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Fans of Dark Matter</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Melissa by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/19528861-haley">Haley</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9684061-melissa?shelf=unforgettable-reads">unforgettable-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9684061-melissa?shelf=great-twist">great-twist</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9684061-melissa?shelf=2019">2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9684061-melissa?shelf=emotional">emotional</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9684061-melissa?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9684061-melissa?shelf=mind-fuck">mind-fuck</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2622956296" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17305850068234802075"><i>Creative. Though-provoking. Emotionally-charged. Memorable.</i><br/><br/>Whether you’re a reader that frequents the sci-fi genre, or one that only occasionally takes a risk when it comes to the suspension of disbelief (<i>hello, that’s me!</i>), recognizing and appreciating the level of creativity behind <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/442240.Blake_Crouch' title='Blake Crouch' rel='nofollow noopener'>Blake Crouch</a>’s work takes little effort. Time and again, Crouch has proven just how rewarding it can be to take a chance on something different. Something totally outside of my typical. With <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1725767587?book_show_action=true&from_review_page=1' rel='nofollow noopener'>Dark Matter</a> (<i>one of my a</i></span>
  <span id="freeText17305850068234802075" style="display:none"><i>Creative. Though-provoking. Emotionally-charged. Memorable.</i><br /><br />Whether you’re a reader that frequents the sci-fi genre, or one that only occasionally takes a risk when it comes to the suspension of disbelief (<i>hello, that’s me!</i>), recognizing and appreciating the level of creativity behind <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/442240.Blake_Crouch" title="Blake Crouch" rel="nofollow noopener">Blake Crouch</a>’s work takes little effort. Time and again, Crouch has proven just how rewarding it can be to take a chance on something different. Something totally outside of my typical. With <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1725767587?book_show_action=true&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Dark Matter</a> (<i>one of my all-time favorite books</i>) and now <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/42046112.Recursion" title="Recursion by Blake Crouch" rel="nofollow noopener">Recursion</a>, Crouch presents readers with a mind-bending reality. While each book provides its own unique and fully immersive journey, they share the provocation of deep thought and emotion on the part of the reader.<br /><br />Fair or not, my feelings for <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1725767587?book_show_action=true&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Dark Matter</a> sent me into <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/42046112.Recursion" title="Recursion by Blake Crouch" rel="nofollow noopener">Recursion</a> with the highest of hopes. Hopes that I thought were going to be shattered early on when focusing felt undoable. A science guru I am <u>not</u>. Wrapping my head around what these characters were trying to achieve with memory recalibration, while simultaneously trying to foreshadow how Crouch would tie the two timelines together, <b>felt taxing on my brain</b>. So much so, I had to take a breath for a few days. Following that brief timeout, I did would I should have from the beginning. Instead of trying to make sense of it all—way too early on—I handed the reins back to Crouch and put my faith in his ability to tell an unforgettable story. And sure enough, along the same vein as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1725767587?book_show_action=true&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Dark Matter</a>, there was no walking away unscathed or unmoved by his words or these characters.<br /><br />The first tease of the storylines converging was all it took for the pitter-patter of this idealistic heart of mine to speed up. And wouldn’t you know, the two characters in question not only managed to steal my heart, but to hold it captive for the entirety of the remaining pages. It was with hope, fear, and bated breath that this lover of love watched the couple’s pilgrimage play out. There’s something to be said for Crouch’s ability to relay a love story of <i>this</i> caliber within such an intricate and science-based thriller. There are romance authors out there who fail to pull off such an unwavering love; one that transcends several iterations, at that. <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>“My soul knows your soul. In any time.”</i>
</blockquote><br /><br />From the very beginning to beyond the final words, Crouch’s exploration of memory, and what it would mean to have the ability to go back and undo those moments that tether our pain, proves to be more than just imaginative fiction.<br /><br /><blockquote><i>Life with a cheat code isn’t life. Our existence isn’t something to be engineered or optimized for the avoidance of pain.<br /><br />That’s what it is to be human—the beauty</i> and <i>the pain, each meaningless without the other.</i></blockquote><br /><br /><i>*Thanks to my #bookbestie Haley for sending me a gorgeous ARC and for ensuring that I didn’t miss out on this mighty piece of fiction. ♥</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="17305850068234802075" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68216634-j-e-w-e-l-s?shelf=recent-faves">recent-faves</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68216634-j-e-w-e-l-s?shelf=books-bejeweled">books-bejeweled</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2763821907" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3077711413702325046"><b>FIVE MIND-BENDING STARS</b><br/><br/>Book readers tend to throw around words like “addictive” and “unputdownable”. But, I'm dead serious about those words. And guys, I’m here to tell you, I read <b>RECURSION</b> straight through dinner last night until I finished at three am this morning. What an intelligent and freakin’ addictive thriller!<br/><br/>The first half sets up the rest of the book and it is crucial to read carefully and try to understand the very simple quantum physics necessary to travel around in time. LOL.😂<br/><br/>I fi</span>
  <span id="freeText3077711413702325046" style="display:none"><b>FIVE MIND-BENDING STARS</b><br /><br />Book readers tend to throw around words like “addictive” and “unputdownable”. But, I'm dead serious about those words. And guys, I’m here to tell you, I read <b>RECURSION</b> straight through dinner last night until I finished at three am this morning. What an intelligent and freakin’ addictive thriller!<br /><br />The first half sets up the rest of the book and it is crucial to read carefully and try to understand the very simple quantum physics necessary to travel around in time. LOL.😂<br /><br />I finally thought I had the timelines straight in my mind (without the use of a giant white board)--I wanted to keep it straight, so I read. And read. And cried. And marveled. And cried again. And closed the Kindle. And kept thinking and marveling and sighing. <br /><br />Who doesn’t want a do-over in life? Personally, I don’t trust anyone that says they live with no regrets. Even if you consider yourself a perfect specimen, I guarantee you have deeply hurt someone’s feelings or perhaps grieved the loss of a loved one. If those aren’t regrets, then you may be a sociopath.<br /><br />What if you could go back through your memories and “fix” them? Change events in order to protect children, countries, civilizations. <br /><br />This is the question <b>RECURSION</b> poses to the reader. As wonderful an idea as this is, there are, of course, consequences to changing history. Blake Crouch turns his incredible imagination loose in his latest thriller and your mind will be racing trying to keep up him.<br /><br /><b>RECURSION</b> is set in 2007 and 2018, this isn’t futuristic. <b>Helene, our genius scientist, works to discover a cure for Alzheimer’s and you will find yourself constantly wondering if this memory recapture business is actually a real thing now. (IT IS. READ THE ACKNOWLEDGEMENTS IN THE BACK!).</b> <br /><br />I love sci-fi that reads like it could be factual. I love sci-fi with colorful, endearing characters. I love sci-fi with the entire world’s future at stake and these two characters must save us. I love sci-fi when those two characters carry on an epic love story to end all love stories. ❤️<br /><br />I love <b>RECURSION</b>. I think I love it more than <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/27833670.Dark_Matter" title="Dark Matter by Blake Crouch" rel="nofollow noopener">Dark Matter</a>. And I never thought I would say that!<br /><br /><i>Hey, all you influential readers: this is still available on NetGalley! Grab it before it is too late! NETFLIX already bought the movie rights and it is gonna be HUGE!!. Many thanks to the publisher and the author for allowing me to read and review the advanced copy of <b> RECURSION</b>. All opinions are mine.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="3077711413702325046" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2858744523" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2858744523" />
    <a title="Petrik" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/59458347-petrik"><img alt="Petrik" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1568016775p2/59458347.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2858744523?book_show_action=true">Jun 18, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Petrik" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Petrik" href="/user/show/59458347-petrik">Petrik</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781984826015" href="/book/show/51794823-recursion">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">sci-fi &amp; Dark Matter fans</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Petrik by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/58160628-emily-books-with-emily-fox">Emily (Books with Emily Fox)</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/59458347-petrik?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2858744523" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3934182327742446652"><b><i>Recursion</i> has become the first sci-fi standalone to be included in my favorite shelves.</b><br/><br/>As many readers probably did, my first experience with reading Crouch’s work was for <i>Dark Matter</i>. I was super impressed by it and after hearing that the author has a new sci-fi thriller that’s highly recommended for readers who loved <i>Dark Matter</i> gave me so much joy; it would be insane for me to not take a look at <i>Recursion</i>. Do note that taking a look at Crouch’s novel can be surmised as reading the novel non-s</span>
  <span id="freeText3934182327742446652" style="display:none"><b><i>Recursion</i> has become the first sci-fi standalone to be included in my favorite shelves.</b><br /><br />As many readers probably did, my first experience with reading Crouch’s work was for <i>Dark Matter</i>. I was super impressed by it and after hearing that the author has a new sci-fi thriller that’s highly recommended for readers who loved <i>Dark Matter</i> gave me so much joy; it would be insane for me to not take a look at <i>Recursion</i>. Do note that taking a look at Crouch’s novel can be surmised as reading the novel non-stop until completion. This book was undoubtedly exceptional; it was so good that it made <i>Dark Matter</i>—which I loved and rated 4.5/5 stars—felt like a practice novel so that Crouch has the skill to unleash the full capacity of his brain towards the creation of this cleverly crafted insanity.<br /><br />Two central characters drive the plot. The first main character is Barry Sutton, a cop that’s investigating the mysterious phenomenon dubbed as False Memory Syndrome (FMS)—a phenomenon that drives its victims insane with false memories of a life they never lived. The other main character, Helena Smith, is a neuroscientist that understands the importance of memory; she decides to dedicate her life to create a technology that could preserve any moment of the recipient’s memories. This is pretty much all I can say regarding the general premise. Reviewing Crouch’s book is not an easy task; there’s a huge limitation on how much of the plot I can talk about unless I risk spoiling something and I don’t want that. To avoid spoilers, I will say this: <i>Recursion</i> is a sci-fi thriller about memories and how precious they are in defining humanity and their sense of identity. Imbued inside this resonating theme was an addictive story about love, loss, ambition, redemption, and life.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“Life is nothing how he expected it would be when he was young and living under the delusion that things could be controlled. Nothing can be controlled. Only endured.” </blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br /><br />When I started this book, I knew I would be thoroughly engaged by it and Crouch exceeded my high expectations brilliantly. Crouch outstandingly proved that he’s super capable of writing a fast-paced story that doesn’t neglect crucial characterizations. <i>Dark Matter</i> was thought-provoking and this book held similar philosophical discussions about life and choices but honestly speaking, <i>Recursion</i> resonated more with me because I believe that Crouch has improved as an author; his prose was extremely well-polished and the characters were more fleshed out. I truly didn’t expect this novel to be this evocative and large-scale. There were moments where I felt genuinely sad, terrified, and heart-warmed by what the characters went through. The poignant thought-provoking passages made me reflect on life; the gradual increase in stakes and scope that eventually became more destructive and global as the story progressed fully stole my attention cover to cover. I’ve been having difficulties in my life, it’s almost as if this book appeared at the right timing to brighten my mood by teaching me how to think better moving forward; I’m truly grateful for it.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote> “Life with a cheat code isn’t life. Our existence isn’t something to be engineered or optimized for the avoidance of pain. That’s what it is to be human—the beauty and the pain, each meaningless without the other.” </blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br /><br /><i>Recursion</i> was relentlessly thrilling, unpredictable, and mind-blowing. Crouch’s narrative was utterly unputdownable, the harrowing events displayed were enormously impactful, and I absolutely loved every moment of reading this vivid magnificence. I can vouch with certainty that <i>Recursion</i> broke a new milestone for me by becoming the first sci-fi standalone to be included in my ‘favorites’ shelves with a full 5/5 stars rating. Read this breathtaking novel as soon as you can. Trust me, you won’t regret it.<br /><br /><i>Sidenote:<br />I heard Recursion is currently being planned for TV series adaptation by Netflix and I'm so excited for it!</i><br /><br /><b>You can order the book from: <u><a href="http://www.bookdepository.com/book/9781524759780/?a_aid=petrikleo" rel="nofollow noopener">Book Depository (Free shipping)</a></u></b><br /><br /><i>You can find <b><u><a href="http://novelnotions.net/2019/06/18/recursion/" rel="nofollow noopener">this</a></u></b> and the rest of my reviews at <b><u><a href="http://novelnotions.net" rel="nofollow noopener">Novel Notions</a></u></b></i></span>
  <a data-text-id="3934182327742446652" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2666497798" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2666497798" />
    <a title="Susanne  Strong" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4514828-susanne-strong"><img alt="Susanne  Strong" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1583087410p2/4514828.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2666497798?book_show_action=true">Jun 05, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Susanne  Strong" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Susanne  Strong" href="/user/show/4514828-susanne-strong">Susanne  Strong</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4514828-susanne-strong?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4514828-susanne-strong?shelf=buddy-read">buddy-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2666497798" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2389996806639015476">3 Stars.<br/> <br/><b>What can I say about Blake Crouch’s new book Recursion? Well, it’s got “a Whole Lotta Crazy Going On!”<br/> <br/>Can you say, do-over? Are your memories to be trusted? What happens if your memories are replaced with new ones and you keep re-living your life over and over? </b><br/> <br/>Just ask NYPD Detective Barry Sutton, whose life has been in tatters for the last several years, ever since the death of his daughter Meghan. When he is called to the scene of a potential suicide, he learns of something called </span>
  <span id="freeText2389996806639015476" style="display:none">3 Stars.<br /> <br /><b>What can I say about Blake Crouch’s new book Recursion? Well, it’s got “a Whole Lotta Crazy Going On!”<br /> <br />Can you say, do-over? Are your memories to be trusted? What happens if your memories are replaced with new ones and you keep re-living your life over and over? </b><br /> <br />Just ask NYPD Detective Barry Sutton, whose life has been in tatters for the last several years, ever since the death of his daughter Meghan. When he is called to the scene of a potential suicide, he learns of something called “False Memory Syndrome.” Ann Peters Voss claims that the life she is living now is not her original, true life. She states that she was once married to someone else and that she had a son and now, in this life, he ceases to exist. At first, Barry finds Ms. Voss’ claims to be incredulous, until the same thing happens to him.<br /> <br />Helena is the Scientist who is responsible for False Memory Syndrome. She finds a way to travel back in time to change memories and in the end, the world. For her, it started innocently, but then doesn’t it always? <br /> <br />Timelines shift, reality becomes obsolete. Human nature takes over.<br /> <br />“Recursion” by Blake Crouch is a novel that was highly intriguing at first, with characters who I was wholly invested in and then became way too technical for me, thereby losing my interest. I personally love Sci-Fi. I read a decent amount of it and tend to watch a lot more Sci Fi on television than anything else, and yet, I felt like Recursion, missed the mark as the novel wore on. The characters are what drew me into the story, yet around the mid-point of the novel the focus on the characters was lost when the timelines kept shifting, which became difficult to keep track of. <br /> <br /><b>What Blake Crouch excelled at in “Dark Matter,” was crafting a well-executed, highly entertaining story about what could have been a difficult subject to understand - and instead he made it extremely easy to comprehend, while including extremely captivating characters to boot. “Dark Matter” was unputdownable! Sadly, “Recursion” was much more difficult to follow and the characters simply didn’t pull me in.</b><br /> <br />I read “Recursion” with my book buddy Kaceey. I think it might be the first true Science Fiction book we have read together. I loved our discussions about it and look forward to seeing how we feel about other Sci Fi books we read in the future.<br /> <br />Thank you to NetGalley, Crown Publishing and Blake Crouch for an arc of this novel in exchange for an honest review.<br /> <br />Published on Goodreads and NetGalley on 6.5.19.</span>

<div id="review_2778994518" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2778994518" />
    <a title="Paromjit" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/38610813-paromjit"><img alt="Paromjit" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2778994518?book_show_action=true">Apr 08, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Paromjit" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Paromjit" href="/user/show/38610813-paromjit">Paromjit</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38610813-paromjit?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38610813-paromjit?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38610813-paromjit?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2778994518" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8411173029491977127">Blake Crouch's latest science fiction thriller is a complex mind messing of a thought provoking read. It is intense, time shifting and asks profound questions of identity, memory, and what it is that makes us human. Just be prepared to find yourself buffeted all over the place. I understand that the novel is going to be filmed, and I am not surprised by this, this is a twisted story that just fizzes with energy and vitality. NYPD police officer Barry Sutton tries but fails to prevent a woman lea</span>
  <span id="freeText8411173029491977127" style="display:none">Blake Crouch's latest science fiction thriller is a complex mind messing of a thought provoking read. It is intense, time shifting and asks profound questions of identity, memory, and what it is that makes us human. Just be prepared to find yourself buffeted all over the place. I understand that the novel is going to be filmed, and I am not surprised by this, this is a twisted story that just fizzes with energy and vitality. NYPD police officer Barry Sutton tries but fails to prevent a woman leaping off a skyscraper. Despairing and distraught, she spoke of false memory syndrome (FMS) with their vibrant and visceral memories and how her son has been erased, but he had never existed. Is FMS a contagion? A deeply troubled Barry, with his own past traumas, sets out on a journey to investigate.<br /><br />Helena Smith is a brilliant neuroscientist carry out cutting edge technology research on memories. A well intentioned woman, her mother is suffering from Alzheimer's disease, which drives Helena's ambition and work on a memory chair, where she can record memories and re-implant them. Her project receives a huge boost when a rich philanthropist injects it with the necessary financial resources, but does he have a darker hidden agenda? Barry and Helena drive the narrative until their paths connect. What are the repercussions of having our memories manipulated and replaced? Is it a worthy desire to replace our painful memories? How does this impact our sense of who we are?<br /><br />Crouch writes a hard hitting, insane, ground shaking thriller, well constructed, full of tension and suspense, that rockets around all over the place with it's ideas and concepts. It certainly holds the reader's attention with ease, although I admit to enjoying Dark Matter more, there are times when this feels slightly more clunky on occasions. Strap yourself in for one hell of a thrill ride, movingly touching on some crucial issues, with its overt agenda of making you think. Many thanks to Pan Macmillan for an ARC.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8411173029491977127" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2668137292" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2668137292" />
    <a title="Debra" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5032725-debra"><img alt="Debra" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1525132364p2/5032725.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2668137292?book_show_action=true">May 06, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Debra" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Debra" href="/user/show/5032725-debra">Debra</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5032725-debra?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2668137292" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3096512530960307174">"He who controls the past controls the future. He who controls the present controls the past."<br/> - George Orwell, 1984<br/><br/>This was a book I had to sit and think about before writing my review, mainly because I had to let it sink it. What would it be like to live your life over again? What would it be like to go back and change past events? How would this action affect your future? How would it affect the future of others? This book is deep and is thought provoking.<br/><br/>Blake Crouch has written a very ambit</span>
  <span id="freeText3096512530960307174" style="display:none">"He who controls the past controls the future. He who controls the present controls the past."<br /> - George Orwell, 1984<br /><br />This was a book I had to sit and think about before writing my review, mainly because I had to let it sink it. What would it be like to live your life over again? What would it be like to go back and change past events? How would this action affect your future? How would it affect the future of others? This book is deep and is thought provoking.<br /><br />Blake Crouch has written a very ambitious and carefully crafted book about memory, preserving memory, shifting reality, and using our memories and dangers associated with altering these things. He does this with skill and finesse. I would have loved to have been a fly on the wall while he was writing this. <br /><br />Neuroscientist Helena Smith has dedicated her life to inventing a device which will preserve our memories. Her intentions are pure. She wants to help her Mother who has Alzheimer’s, she wants to help those experience their happy times once again. But what happens when people begin experiencing False Memory Syndrome - a syndrome that causes irrational behavior in those who experience memories of lives they never lived.<br /><br />NYC police officer Barry Sutton begins to investigate the syndrome, he learns that there is more going on than meets the eye (or memory). As he digs deeper, he becomes more involved until he is knee deep in neuroscience, time, memories and a lifetime of trying to get things right.<br /><br />I highly recommend making note of the date/YEAR on each chapter as this book is told in both timelines. Things jump around a bit and can be confusing if you are not on your toes keeping track of your time lines. This is a book I really needed to sit and ponder after reading. I found that the more I thought about this book, the more I enjoyed it.<br /><br />Blake Crouch has a brilliant creative mind and he puts it to good use in this book. The beginning of this book was work for me until I found my rhythm with this book. Fans of his previous book <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/27833670.Dark_Matter" title="Dark Matter by Blake Crouch" rel="nofollow noopener">Dark Matter</a> will enjoy this one as well. I did enjoy Dark Matter more mainly because I found it was easier to follow but his one is good, but it took a little more (okay, a lot more) work on my part.<br /><br />I also loved that not only is this science fiction it is also a love story and Crouch writes some beautiful passages such as “...I want to breathe the same air as you every minute of every day of my life, no matter how many timelines I live." and "My soul knows your soul in any time line."<br /><br />Science Fiction fans, Crouch will not let you down with this book. Read those chapters headers and keep them in mind while reading each chapter as time does jump around. <br /><br />Thank you to Crown Publishing and NetGalley who provided me with a copy of this book in exchange for an honest review. All the thoughts and opinions are my own.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3096512530960307174" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2780914029" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2780914029" />
    <a title="Meredith" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30978160-meredith"><img alt="Meredith" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1423329725p2/30978160.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2780914029?book_show_action=true">Sep 02, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Meredith" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Meredith" href="/user/show/30978160-meredith">Meredith</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30978160-meredith?shelf=overdrive">overdrive</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2780914029" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6740480762099976520">4.5 stars<br/><br/><b>
  <i>“There is no past.”<br/><br/>Recursion is a provocative and mind-bending read about nonlinear time, the fluidity of memory, and the power of love. </i>
</b><br/><br/><i>In Recursion</i>, a scientific invention allows for one to go back in time and save a life or prevent a tragic event from occurring. But changing the past has serious consequences in the present. False Memory Syndrome emerges resulting in suicides, bombings, and nuclear war. To stop the destruction of the chair, multiple timelines are created, leading </span>
  <span id="freeText6740480762099976520" style="display:none">4.5 stars<br /><br /><b>
  <i>“There is no past.”<br /><br />Recursion is a provocative and mind-bending read about nonlinear time, the fluidity of memory, and the power of love. </i>
</b><br /><br /><i>In Recursion</i>, a scientific invention allows for one to go back in time and save a life or prevent a tragic event from occurring. But changing the past has serious consequences in the present. False Memory Syndrome emerges resulting in suicides, bombings, and nuclear war. To stop the destruction of the chair, multiple timelines are created, leading to ultimate chaos.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>“Perhaps memory is fundamental, the thing from which time emerges.”</i>
</b><br /><br /><b>This is a fast-paced, action-packed, fascinating read that had me constantly examining my beliefs about memory and time. The writing is sharp, intricately plotted and surprisingly clear. </b><br /><br /> The plot is dense but manageable. While there are multiple timelines and events to keep track of, the structure of the novel made it possible to not get lost. The narrative is divided up into 5 parts, all of which focus on the aftereffects of the memory experiment. Told through the eyes of Barry, an NYPD Detective, and Helena, a scientist, their constant presence put me at ease and offered the clarity I needed when I got lost in trying to understand the science behind the shifts in time.<br /><br />This could have been an overwhelming convoluted mess, but Crouch has the ability to seamless tie all of the many threads together. There were parts when the science went way above my head--I will never fully grasp quantum physics, but I appreciated how this book had me continuously thinking. <i>
  <b>Recursion had my mind spinning and left me with my brain hurting. I don’t read a lot of Science Fiction and this book took me out of my comfort zone--it was well worth reading and I highly recommend! </b>
</i><br /><br /><br /><br /> </span>
  <a data-text-id="6740480762099976520" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2834605781" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2834605781" />
    <a title="BernLuvsBooks " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3087404-bernluvsbooks"><img alt="BernLuvsBooks " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1585010050p2/3087404.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2834605781?book_show_action=true">Jun 10, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="BernLuvsBooks " class="user" itemprop="url" name="BernLuvsBooks " href="/user/show/3087404-bernluvsbooks">BernLuvsBooks </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3087404-bernluvsbooks?shelf=adult-reads">adult-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3087404-bernluvsbooks?shelf=2019">2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3087404-bernluvsbooks?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2834605781" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9807659554551577697"><b>Blake Crouch has done it again!!! <i><u>Recursion</u> was fascinating, confusing and brilliant!<i></i></i></b><br/><br/>Dark Matter is one of my favorite sci-fi books of all time so I was almost scared to delve into Recursion - nervous it wouldn't live up to my expectations for Crouch. This book was ambitious. Thankfully, I had nothing to fear. Mr. Crouch's brilliant mind hasn't failed us yet. <br/><br/>Recursion deals with memory - preserving memory, and using it to shift our reality. What a roller coaster ride this was. Can you imagine g</span>
  <span id="freeText9807659554551577697" style="display:none"><b>Blake Crouch has done it again!!! <i><u>Recursion</u> was fascinating, confusing and brilliant!<i></i></i></b><br /><br />Dark Matter is one of my favorite sci-fi books of all time so I was almost scared to delve into Recursion - nervous it wouldn't live up to my expectations for Crouch. This book was ambitious. Thankfully, I had nothing to fear. Mr. Crouch's brilliant mind hasn't failed us yet. <br /><br />Recursion deals with memory - preserving memory, and using it to shift our reality. What a roller coaster ride this was. Can you imagine going back into a specific memory with all the knowledge you have now? What would you change or do differently if given the opportunity for a "do over"? <br /><br />Barry Sutton is a NYPD Detective who answers a "jumper" call. As he attempts to talk her down from the ledge he learns she is suffering from False Memory Syndrome - vivid memories of an alternate life. These memories feel real and those suffering from FMS have difficulty reconciling the dual memories/lives. <br /><br />Meanwhile, neuroscientist Helena Smith has devoted her life to memory research. She wants to map memories to preserve them. Her greatest hope is to help people with Alzheimers, Dementia and brain injuries. Ultimately she uncovers more than just a way to map memories. Her research leads to the discovery that causes FMS. Helena and her researchers travel back into past memories. This leads to changes which cause dual timeline memories for everyone involved. <br /><br />Barry and Helena's stories intersect as they find themselves face to face with the darker implications of the research. Each change comes with a cost. As more and more people suffer from FMS, mass hysteria builds. Are our minds strong enough to handle dual realities? Can multiple timeline memories coexist in the same person? Can the world handle this type of technology? <br /><br /><b>Recursion certainly made me think and question everything I know about reality. I couldn't help but wonder about those moments of deja vu we all experience. What if there was more to them?</b> Ultimately our memories make up who we are. They are definitely powerful and I love how Crouch explored this topic. It was thought provoking, emotional and made for fascinating reading.<br /><br /><i>A huge thank you to Blake Crouch, Crown Publishing and Netgalley for the opportunity to read &amp; review an arc of this book.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="9807659554551577697" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2899680745" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2899680745" />
    <a title="Barbie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/90413527-barbie"><img alt="Barbie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1601722083p2/90413527.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2899680745?book_show_action=true">Jul 17, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Barbie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Barbie" href="/user/show/90413527-barbie">Barbie</a>
      </span>

        rated it

  <span id="freeText12780129309632020886" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1551534793i/27143282._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b> My thoughts in a nutshell </b><br>I chose Recursion to be my first read by Blake Crouch and I definitely didn't regret it. I can't imagine what it would be like if it actually happened.<br>I adored that fact how much work and effort Blake could put into it. <br>I have only one issue about it. I felt some part extremely repetitive and overwritten. I know, it was necessary but you can't guess how bored I was. It was a real struggle. The ending was too ideal and it reminded me of a perfect Hollywood movie.<br>Overall, if you want to read a good sciency book, I would recommend it.</span>

<div id="review_2837796786" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2837796786" />
    <a title="Tucker  (TuckerTheReader)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/70951605-tucker-tuckerthereader"><img alt="Tucker  (TuckerTheReader)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1594344467p2/70951605.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2837796786?book_show_action=true">May 28, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tucker  (TuckerTheReader)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tucker  (TuckerTheReader)" href="/user/show/70951605-tucker-tuckerthereader">Tucker  (TuckerTheReader)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Tucker  by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/52535740-blake-crouch">Blake Crouch</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/70951605-tucker-tuckerthereader?shelf=arc-physical">arc-physical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/70951605-tucker-tuckerthereader?shelf=dystopian">dystopian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/70951605-tucker-tuckerthereader?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/70951605-tucker-tuckerthereader?shelf=adult">adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/70951605-tucker-tuckerthereader?shelf=favorites-2019">favorites-2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/70951605-tucker-tuckerthereader?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2837796786" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16850197935397507832"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1559083466i/27585460._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><i>Many thanks to Crown Books for sending me a copy in exchange for an honest review</i><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1578275103i/28718284.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>This book was sent to me by the publisher! If you would like to know how to get ARCs and review copies, feel free to watch my video, <a href='https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=XdlypQbFcl0&feature=youtu.be' rel='nofollow noopener'>Advanced Reader Copies 101</a>! <br/><br/>----------<br/><br/><b>[12/10/19]</b> - Congratulations, Blake Crouch, on winning the 2019 Goodreads Choice Award for Science Fiction!<br/><br/>----------<br/><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote>re·cur·sion<br/>/re-ker-zhun/<br/>noun<br/>the repeated application of a recursive procedure or definition.</blockquote>
  </b>
</i><br/>Have you ever had one of th</span>
  <span id="freeText16850197935397507832" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1559083466i/27585460._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>Many thanks to Crown Books for sending me a copy in exchange for an honest review</i><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1578275103i/28718284.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>This book was sent to me by the publisher! If you would like to know how to get ARCs and review copies, feel free to watch my video, <a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=XdlypQbFcl0&amp;feature=youtu.be" rel="nofollow noopener">Advanced Reader Copies 101</a>! <br><br>----------<br><br><b>[12/10/19]</b> - Congratulations, Blake Crouch, on winning the 2019 Goodreads Choice Award for Science Fiction!<br><br>----------<br><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote>re·cur·sion<br>/re-ker-zhun/<br>noun<br>the repeated application of a recursive procedure or definition.</blockquote>
  </b>
</i><br>Have you ever had one of those books that literally change the way you look at life? Well, if you haven't, you don't know what your missing. <i>Recursion</i> is one of those books that you don't completely understand but.. You do at the same time. You know what I'm saying? Anyway, I don't have a good translation so ON TO THE CHARACTER ANALYSIS:<br><br>➵ <b>Barry</b> - Barry, a police officer (in one timeline, that is 😏) who's daughter has recently passed away. Throughout the book, he deals with grief and guilt as aftermath of his daughter's death. One day, he is given the chance to redo the day his daughter died and he takes it, ending up saving her daughter. He begins to feel uncomfortable, feeling as though he's muddled with something he shouldn't have. Little does he know how right he is...<br><br>➵ <b>Helena</b> - Helena is the genius who invents The Chair, which is basically a time-traveling troublemaker. She too deals with guilt as her invention is used for purposes not intended. Her strength and endurance is shown as she does whatever it takes to rectify the problem she caused, no matter what it takes.<br><br>Science fiction is one of my favorite genres. Since I was young, I have always loved seeing authors take real, hard facts and adding a dash of magic to them. It's been a while since I read a hardy science fiction. This did not disappoint. I didn't realize how much I missed getting shaky from excitement because I could see all the pieces fitting together. Even worse, I am now ruined for all other science victim because this was so well written.<br><br>In <i>Recursion</i>, we follow the invention of The Chair which allows you to travel back to your memories and rewrite them. This is based on the idea that the present moment is an illusion. To put it simply, by the time our brains process stimuli, whatever sent that stimuli is already in the past. I did not realize that and when I did, I f**king lost it. I mean... People.. We are always getting old data and stimuli! Everything we see, hear, and feel is already in the past... AUUUGHHH. It's absolutely crazy! <br><br>Anyway, slowly people start to realize the existence of the Chair and what it can do. And then... The sh*t hits the fan. Time travel happens and people's minds get f**ked up because the timelines are blending together and humanity cannot handle the mental toll. Now, Barry and Helena join forces in hopes of destroying the Chair.<br><br>I think the best part of the book is that, because time gets royally screwed up, this book is told kind of our order making it confusing but simple at the same time. Blake Crouch uses the idea of time to his advantage and weaves a stunningly beautiful story. When (not if because you must read this book) you read this, you will find yourself not wanting it to end.<br><br>Finally, I cannot recommend this book enough. It's one of those books that no review could ever do it justice. You need to experience it yourself.<br><br>Bottom Line:<br>4.5 Stars<br>Age Rating [ R ]<br>TW: Suicide, Graphic Content<br>Reps: [None]<br>Cover: 5/5 ~ Characters: 4/5 ~ Plot: 5/5 ~ Audio:4/5<br>Publication Date: June 11th, 2019<br>Publisher: Crown Books<br>Genre: Thriller/Science Fiction<br><br> <br>| <a href="https://Goodreads.com/tuckeralmengor" rel="nofollow noopener">Goodreads</a> | <a href="https://tuckerthereader.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://Pinterest.com/tuckeralmengor" rel="nofollow noopener">Pinterest</a> | <a href="https://linkedin.com/in/tuckeralmengor" rel="nofollow noopener">LinkedIn</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/channel/UC1JLAbHwaeQ5YwayF3UhjWw" rel="nofollow noopener">YouTube</a> | <a href="https://instagram.com/tuckeralmengor" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a></span>
